Cleaning the razor is amazingly easy too; as you can simply remove the foil, add soap directly to the blades, and clean the shaver in seconds, using the built in 'sonic vibration cleaning mode', which ups the CPM (cycles per minute) from 13,000 to 17,000, and will literally vibrate any debris free from the blades. The convenience is you can do this while in the shower, as the entire shaver is waterproof. Charging is also amazing, as the shaver can be recharged in under an hour, and that charge will last through the entire week. Another feature I love is the travel lock on the power button. This prevents the shaver from coming on unintentionally while packed away in a bag, if the power button in accidentally depressed. The case it comes with is a nice fabric pouch, that keeps in easily protected (though I still pack it in a shoe when traveling). Panasonic recommends giving your face 30 days to adjust to the shaver; but as a 'typical guy' with sensitive skin; I was sold from day one. I cannot recommend this higher. Hope this helps.

  109. This shaver works great for me. For the past few years, I've been shaving with a disposable in the shower. I have pretty sensitive skin, and figured all that hot water would help soften my beard and make the whole process easier, although I was still getting some redness and irritation afterwards. When I got this wet/dry shaver, I used it in the shower the first few times, and it worked very well, but then I decided to try it dry. For me, it was an eye-opener, because I was actually able to shave more quickly, and without any irritation. I've been using it dry ever since, a little over a month now. I feel like it has \\"liberated\\" me from shower shaving; now I can just grab it and get a quick shave anytime I want.<br /><br />The shaver has a very \\"cool\\" look, but more importantly, it has some nice features. It only takes one hour to fully charge the battery, and though I haven't tested this myself, the instructions say a full charge will give you up to 45 minutes (approximately 2 weeks) of cordless shaving. A 5-minute quick charge = 1 shave.<br /><br />It has a flexible, pivoting head, with a switch to select either \\"locked\\" or \\"soft\\" (\\"soft\\" allows it to pivot, which is how I always use it). There is also a lock ring on the front of the razor to lock the power switch while carrying/storing the shaver.<br /><br />It has a pop-up trimmer. It also comes with a little velveteen bag to carry or store it in.<br /><br />The LCD panel on the front of the unit displays in a bright amber, which is nice (easy to read, even without my glasses). It shows the battery capacity and the charge status. It will also show a reminder when it's time to use the sonic vibration cleaning mode. To do that, you apply some liquid hand soap and water to the outer foil (while it's on the shaver), and press the power switch for more than 2 seconds, which activates the sonic cleaning mode (you hear a high-pitch sound as the blades vibrate super fast). It shuts itself off after 20 seconds, then youremove the foil section, activate the sonic mode once more while holding the blades under running water to rinse. It's quick and easy to do.<br /><br />Sometimes I do have to go over my neck area a few extra times to get it perfectly smooth, and even then, I might notice later that it still missed a whisker here and there, especially if I haven't shaved in a couple of days. But that was the case too when I was using a disposable in the shower, and even more so, actually.<br /><br />When I'm through shaving, I remove the foil head and rinse it and the blades under running water. Again, quick and easy.<br /><br />I should mention that there is no stand or cradle to put the shaver in while it's charging; you plug one end of the cord into the base of the shaver, and the other end -- a piece measuring about 2\\" x 2\\" x 1\\" thick -- plugs into an outlet. A stand or cradle might have been nice, but this configuration hasn't been a problem for me.<br /><br />Just as an aside, another reviewer mentioned that he tried to use this shaver with shaving foam, and it just created a mess. If this is true for you, you might consider trying the Alba Botanica Moisturizing Foam Shave. [[ASIN:B000IM5AX2 Moisturizing Foam Shave Sea Mist - 5 - Fluid Oz.]] The reason I think this might work better, is because, despite the name, it's not actually a \\"foam\\" like the conventional ones in cans. It comes out of the dispenser as a light foam, but virtually disappears when applied to the face. However, it seems to have an oil base that really allows the razor/shaver to glide smoothly. If you've ever used the Shaving Oil drops like they sell at the drugstore or supermarket, it's akin to those. It's just a very slight foam that provides good lubrication. It's what I used with disposable razors to shave in the shower, and it did work well with this shaver the few times I used it in the shower. Just thought I'd mention that.<br /><br />I'm very pleased with this shaver, and happy that it freed me from myshower-shaving habit!

In this case, the 13k cycle per minute cutting rate combined with the blade system, ergonomics, and price point will likely place this in the sweet spot for most users. The [[ASIN:B005DKKBRY Panasonic ES-LT41-K Men's 3-Blade (Arc 3) Wet/Dry Rechargeable Electric Shaver with Nanotech Blades, Black/Silver]] does not come with a cleaning system or charging stand; hence the reason for lower price when compared to products like the [[ASIN:B00176V2SK Panasonic ES8228S Men's Linear Vortex Nano Arc Foil Shaving System, Silver]]. The battery will fully charge in 70 minutes (at least that was my measured rate) and retain the charge for weeks. As with these types of batteries, let the battery run completely down before charging the first few times. This will condition the battery and extend its like significantly. The LCD is simply fabulous and easy to read. It primarily shows the battery and cleaning status. I have friends who swear by rotary heads as opposed the foil types (this type). Another point with foil versus rotary head razors is irritation, which I infrequently experience but some friends experience at a far greater rate. Also, for anyone looking to get as close of a shave as with products like the [[ASIN:B000BUUVTE Gillette Fusion Manual Razor]], simply forget it despite what other may say. I have never experienced as close of a shave. For many, that may take some getting used to. In my neck area for example, I often have to make repeat passes at various angles (my hair will often grow in at weird angles). Finally, if you are someone who lets your beard grow out at length before shaving, this razor, and most electric razors are not for you.<br /><br />I gave this razor 5 stars based on its design, quality, usefulness, and price point at the sub-$75 range.   220. I've been a long time Braun customer, my last Braun shaver (Braun Contour 5790) has lasted for approximately 11 years. I was very hesitant on changing to a different brand or shaver type, but I researched for a while on the current rotory & foil shavers and have settled on the Panasonic ES-LT41-K. I was very close to pulling the trigger on another Braun in the same price range (Series 3-530cc), but many of the reviews claim that the Braun shavers have been inconsistent with shaving &#34;closeness/smoothness&#34;. Also, per reviews the Braun build quality and included accessories seems to be dropping as of late. I simply cannot justify spending more money just to have the accessories included or to improve the actual shaving quality when other brands can provide these improvements and accessories for a lower price.<br /><br />After using the Panasonic ES-LT41-K, I immediately noticed a few key differences, it has a slightly louder & higher pitched sound than the Braun shavers. It's lighter in weight, and more comfortable to hold. The shaver-head lock, power-button lock, and LCD display features are nice upgrades that you typically pay more for with Braun shavers and it includes a protective plastic foil-cover and a storage bag for travel. The cleaning method is a little more echonomical, since you can use either water or water and liquid/gel anti-bacterial soap vs buying a cleaning cartridge for the Braun cleaning system. Panasonic does sell foil shavers with an included cleaning system, but why go out of your way to buy it and then have to pay for the cleaning supplies when you can go without.<br /><br />The only drawbacks that I've noticed with the Panasonic ES-LT41-K is that the foil/blade replacement parts are more expensive than Brauns, and you cannot use the shaver while it's charging (for water/electrical safety reasons, being that this is a wet/dry shaver). My Braun contour 5790 was a wet/dry shaver (although I never used it in the shower), and it could be used while it was charging. I'm not sure if Braun sells any newer models that offer this feature (it has proven useful many times in the past, when the battery was dead/low), but nowadays it seems that most wet/dry shavers, including the Braun shavers, have disabled the &#34;use while charging&#34; feature.<br /><br />My first shave with the Panasonic ES-LT41-K was on 3-day old facial hair. I wanted to try it on a worst case senario, any thing longer than this should be trimmed first with a beard trimmer to prevent most shaving issues with any electric shaver. Most electric shavers are not designed to handle beard growth more than 3-4 days. I noticed that with a 3-day old beard the shaver worked best with a light touch to simply trim the beard down to a more manageable length, then go over the entire area once more with a slight pressure to get the closest shave. Prior to this final pass, I also used Williams Lectric Shave. The shave was overall quicker, slightly less irritating (with 3-day old beard), and had fewer missed hairs than the older Braun shaver. I will admit that the blades/foil on the Braun were past their prime, and this can contribute to a loss of performance.<br /><br />As for the trimmer attachement, Both the Panasonic and Braun trimmer attachments could have been made better and performed about the same. My Braun trimmer attachment fell apart after about 3 years. I no longer rely on the integrated trimmers and have a separate beard trimmer to handle the trimming job properly. The Braun and the Panasonic were in my opinion equal at giving a close/smooth shave when the foil/blades are new. Overall, I am very satisfied with the performance of both shavers, with the Panasonic slightly out edging the Braun because of less irritation with longer facial hair.<br /><br />The cleaning process for the Panasonic ES-LT41-K was very simple and took very little time. Remove the foil then press and hold the power button for 2 seconds to activatethe cleaning mode (higher frequency). Then pass the blade portion of the shaver under cool tap water until the shavings are rinsed off. Rinse the foil separately under cool water, shake to remove most of the moisture and then air dry before reinstalling onto the shaver. To help dry the shaver, re-activate the cleaning mode to shake off most of the moisture. Wipe away the residual moisture from the shaver housing (not really necessary), and then air dry separately from the foil. Reinstall the foil when everything is dry prior to your next shave. Once per week or per recharge, add liquid/gel anti-bacterial soap to the foil while it is installed over the blades and turn on the shaver to help lather up the soap and clean the metal surfaces. Remove the foil and rinse the foil and blades separately under cool tap water. Only activate the cleaning mode while rinsing or drying the blades with the foil removed from the shaver.

  263. In the past, I used a Remington rotary shaver and it felt like my hairs were being pulled, instead of cut. In the end, my skin suffered. Therefore, I was done with electric razors. Then, after using the messy [[ASIN:B0048ZIFA0 Soft Sheen Carson Magic Fragrant Shaving Powder]], which can only be used 36 hours after an initial shave, I went to using razors, such as the [[ASIN:B003987CL0 Gillette Fusion Proglide Power Razor, 1-count Package]]. However, the cartridges were too pricey, so I would try to prolong them by shaving, twice a week. Therefore, I figured I would try some kind of electric razor, so I could get a good shave, everyday. This time, I was looking for a foil shaver because the rotary shaver irritated my skin. Then, I discovered the high ratings of the Panasonic Arc three on Amazon and decided to try it.<br /><br />Features: This electric shaver is very versatile. It can be used wet or dry. In fact, regular shaving cream can be used with this shaver. The flexible pivoting head allows for a more precise shave around the contours of your face. The shaver can also be used, without the heads pivoting because there is a \\"lock\\" switch, which keeps the heads steady, during shaving. The pop-up trimmer is surprisingly effective. It actually trims better than my Remington trimmers. It trims the side burns and beard very quickly and surprisingly close. Other pop-up trimmers seemed useless, compared to this one. Keep in mind, the heads may block your vision on the desired areas to trim. Therefore, turning the shaver in a way to get a better look on where you want to trim should help.<br /><br />Performance: The 30 degree Nanotech blades gives a fairly close shave, depending on how your hair grows. Don't expect the blades to shave very close after just one pass, ESPECIALLY if the hair that is thick. With that being said, I would recommend using this shaver, when the hair is not very thick. Of course, using the shaver, everyday or every other day should help, as well. Either way, a smooth and comfortable shave will be the aftermath of complete use.<br /><br />Cleaning: Cleaning this shaver could not have been easier. After shaving, just put some hand soap on the foils of the shaver. Turn the shaver on and wait for the soap to lather. Remove the foil. Then, rinse the blades and the foil with water. It is that simple. For a more intense cleaning, you can use the Sonic Vibration Mode. Just press and hold the power button for a few seconds and the blades will vibrate, vigorously. Then, hold the blades under water and any access hair caught up in the shaver will be rinsed and shaken away.<br /><br />Charging: A full charge only takes and hour. Also, this shaver can be used for 45min. of cordless shaving. It also has a five-minute quick charge feature, which allows just one shave, when the power has been exhausted. Of course, this would only be necessary if you were in a hurry to get a quick shave. The percentage of the charge can be see on the illuminated indicator on the front of the shaver.<br /><br />This is a very good and versatile shaver. The only downside to this shaver is it does not cut close, without a number passes. The other issue with this shaver is it cannot be used, while it is plugged up. Of course, that is not a major flaw. Overall, this shaver is worth owning, especially for the price it has dropped to.<br /><br />Exactly one year, later........<br /><br />In the owners manual, the creators have a strong clam that the user won't have the desire to shave with anything else, if used for a minimum of 30 days. Of course, they claim this is the duration for a person's face to get used to various methods of shaving. Prior to that minimum of 30 days, I was not totally satisfied because of impatience, but the more I shaved, I realized that they were right. This shaver has totally cleared up my skin on my neck area. After using a razor for months, my skin was smooth, but it had somewhat of an irritated look on my neck area.Now, that is ALL cleared up. People have also noticed the difference in how smooth my skin is, since I have been consistently using this shaver. This tells me that the shaver is good for people with sensitive skin. If you buy this shaver and have any reservations after using it a couple of times, give it at the very minimum, 30 day chance. After owning this shaver for a whole year, it is still gives me a very comfortable shave. I will NEVER shave with anything else, again.Now, that is ALL cleared up.   334. I've used electric shavers for the last 50 years. I've owned most models, from Ronson and Remington to Braun, Norelco and Panasonic, wired and rechargeable, with rotary, foil and bar cutters. None have topped my recent Panasonic ES-8068. But at 12 years old, it was starting to show its age. Its charged lifespan went from 6 days down to 2. And parts were getting more difficult to obtain, particularly the pop-up trimmer. So, I elected to replace it with the ES-LT41. I've used the ES-LT41 daily for the past 2 weeks and I've formed some early opinions. First, it's lighter in weight compared to the ES-8068. That makes it easier to hold but it doesn't have the same heft. I'm hoping the weight-savings aren't the result of less sturdy construction or of a lighter and smaller battery but I'm not holding my breath. Second, the ES-LT41 is more difficult to push through my stubble, whereas the ES-8068 moved smoothly across my face and objected only when presented with a 2-day growth of beard. The ES-LT41 reminds me of the Norelco rotary shaver I once owned and gave away because of my feeling that I had to &#34;push&#34; it through my beard. The ES-LT41 feels the same way. Once it gets the rough stubble down to a shorter length, though, the ES-LT41 does a very good job of getting all the hairs removed down to the smooth skin. In this regard, it's as good as the ES-8068 was on its best day. Third, the flexible head seems like a gimmick. It's not actually needed, as I've tried the shaver in both the &#34;locked&#34; and &#34;soft&#34; positions and seen no difference in how well either mode performed. And the flexibility has no discernible advantage (other than marketing) and may just introduce unneccessary mechanical and electrical complications. So, I'm still undecided about this razor. Sure, it gives a close shave but so did my ES-8068 when it was brand new. Both use the &#34;linear&#34; motor at 13,000rpm, yet the ES-LT41 is a bit quieter than the ES-8068, perhaps because it's a later design. The ES-LT41 is cheaper than my old ES-8068, by a long-shot, which may account for my perception that I've &#34;stepped down&#34; in class. I guess the only way I'll know is if it lasts me 12 years. If anything changes, I'll update this review. Update April 2015: This has lasted all of 2 years and has done a fairly decent job. However, now the trimmer won't work. The trimmer engagement is made of cheap plastic and the arm that oscillates the cutter has popped out of place and doesn't engage the cutting head. No amount of coaxing will move it back into place. Panasonic used to be my preferred shaver but no more. I'm sick of decent products cheapened in order to increase the profit margin. I expected better than this. No more Panasonic; I'm off to check out the Braun shavers. But my expectations are lower, given that this is what the market now offers.

I almost never get any razor burn or in-grown hairs, whereas I do get these with razors. It takes a few extra minutes to complete the shave compared to razor (maybe 7-8 min vs. 5-6 min). Simply put, when confronted with an opportunity to switch to another manufacturer when my previous razor finally stopped working, I stayed with the Panasonic line.<br /><br />Comparison of ES-LT41K to ES-8103S<br />The product comparison chart shows the two shavers to be nearly identical - and they are. the LT41 has an added travel lock, which is a nice feature, although I had never had problems with my 8103 turning on during travel. However, there are some notable differences that I believe are improvements with the LT41 line.<br /><br />&#62; First the feel of the shaver has been improved through the addition of a more textured plastic material. This helps with control of the shaver during use.<br />&#62; The power screen is perhaps less reflective or something - I find it easier to read.<br />&#62; The power consumption / capacity thus far has been identical for the equivalent new units.<br />&#62; Weight of the LT41 seems to have been reduced slightly - although I never had fatigue from weight using the 8103.<br />&#62; Charge times are not noticeable different, perhaps a bit faster with the LT41<br />&#62; Price: ~ 5% lower cost with the LT41 at the time of my purchase.<br /><br />Summary: Great shaver, highly recommended. A few nice but modest upgrades from the ES-8103S line.feel of the shaver has been improved through the addition of a more textured plastic material.   353. Seldom have I been so happy with a purchase. This shaver has been very well designed to shave well, clean easily, and maintain. It does require a learning process to use intelligently. One cannot just fly over the whiskers like an ordinary razor. One gets better results by going over the skin at a snail's pace, allowing the skin to compress, unroll, and conform to the shape of the razor head, thus presenting the whiskers at maximum advantage to the blades for best &#34;off with her head&#34; performance. So I shave like King Henry, ok. Also, feeling the whiskers remaining as you go helps align the stroke with the best direction for cutting performance, as you seek the lay of the whiskers to approach from the opposite direction. After shave is essential for me to prevent infection after this close a shave. The skin toughens up after a few months, and the result is a very close shave every day. Well worth the price. Only one note: the shaver head comes out of the detachable mount, and I did not know that. Accidently pushed the metal head and plastic mount assembly out and it fell into the drain. Luckily, I had the tools to retrieve it, but now I am very careful to handle that removeable head with no chance of dropping it. All in all, an excellent buy, and if I lose this one, or wear it out, I would buy another.
